# LoCoBench-Agent Task

## Task Information

**Task ID**: rust_web_social_expert_073_architectural_understanding_expert_01

## Task Title

Architectural Analysis for Real-time Feature Integration in an Event-Driven System

## Description

EduPulse Live is a complex, event-driven social learning platform built in Rust. The system architecture is highly modularized to handle features like user authentication, study group management, content searching, and session management. The source code is spread across numerous modules with non-descriptive names (e.g., `module_1.txt`, `module_2.txt`), requiring deep code analysis to understand their purpose. The core of the system relies on an event bus for communication between components, following patterns like CQRS (Command Query Responsibility Segregation). The company now wants to introduce a highly interactive 'Real-time Collaborative Whiteboard' feature for study groups. As a senior architect, your task is to analyze the existing architecture to determine the best integration strategy and identify potential challenges.

## Your Task

Your task is to perform a thorough architectural analysis and create a strategic plan for integrating a new 'Real-time Collaborative Whiteboard' feature. You must not write any implementation code. Your response should be a detailed report based on your understanding of the existing codebase.

1.  **Identify Core Architectural Components:** Analyze the provided files (`config.txt`, `package.json`, and `src/module_*.txt` files) to identify and describe the roles of the key components in the existing event-processing pipeline. Specifically, identify the modules responsible for:
    *   API Gateway / Handling incoming HTTP requests.
    *   User Authentication and Session Management.
    *   Publishing commands/events to the message bus.
    *   Consuming events to update data stores (write models).
    *   Serving read-optimized data (query models).

2.  **Trace an Existing Data Flow:** Describe the complete lifecycle of a user creating a new post in a study group. Trace this action from the initial API call through the event bus to the final data persistence, naming the specific modules (`module_XX.txt`) involved at each stage.

3.  **Propose an Integration Strategy:** Design a high-level architectural solution for the 'Real-time Collaborative Whiteboard' feature. Your proposal must address:
    *   The mechanism for handling low-latency, real-time communication (e.g., drawing actions) between clients.
    *   The new service(s) or module(s) required.
    *   How whiteboard state will be persisted without compromising the performance of the core application.
    *   How the new feature will integrate with the existing user authentication and event bus.

4.  **Visualize the Architecture:** Generate two diagrams in MermaidJS `graph TD` format:
    *   **Diagram 1:** The existing architecture, showing the flow you traced in step 2.
    *   **Diagram 2:** The proposed architecture, incorporating the new Collaborative Whiteboard components.

5.  **Identify Architectural Risks:** List and explain the top 3 potential architectural risks or bottlenecks associated with your proposed integration. Focus on performance, scalability, and data consistency.

## Expected Approach

An expert developer would start by examining configuration and dependency files for high-level clues, then dive into the source code to confirm hypotheses and map out the system.

1.  **Initial Reconnaissance:** The developer would first inspect `package.json` to identify key dependencies like `axum` (web framework), `tokio` (async runtime), `sqlx` (database), `serde` (serialization), and a message bus client like `nats` or `lapin` (for RabbitMQ). They would then check `src/config.txt` for service URLs (e.g., NATS server address, multiple database connection strings suggesting CQRS), secret keys, and other configuration that defines the environment.

2.  **Pattern Identification:** The developer would scan the `src/module_*.txt` files for recurring patterns and keywords. They would look for `axum::Router` to find the API entry points, structs with `#[derive(Serialize, Deserialize)]` that look like `Events` or `Commands`, functions that `publish` to a message bus, and functions that `subscribe` or `handle` messages. This helps categorize the opaque modules.

3.  **Component Mapping:** By combining clues from dependencies and code patterns, the developer would map modules to roles. For example, a module that sets up an `axum::Router` and calls an authentication function is likely the API Gateway. Modules with functions that handle structs named `CreatePostCommand` are command handlers. Modules that handle `PostCreatedEvent` and perform `sqlx` database writes are event consumers/denormalizers.

4.  **Tracing and Diagramming:** The developer would trace a specific command, like creating a post, by finding the API endpoint, seeing which command it generates, finding the handler for that command, seeing which event the handler emits, and finally finding the consumer for that event. This flow would be translated into a MermaidJS diagram.

5.  **Solution Design:** For the new feature, the expert would recognize that standard event bus patterns are too high-latency for real-time drawing. They would propose a dedicated WebSocket service. This service would handle the WebSocket connections, broadcasting drawing data directly to clients in a specific 'room' or 'session'. For persistence, they would suggest snapshotting the whiteboard state to the primary database periodically, while perhaps using a faster cache like Redis for transient actions. This new service would still hook into the main event bus for authentication and to be notified when a study session starts or ends.

## Evaluation Criteria

- **Component Identification Accuracy:** How accurately did the agent identify the roles of the key modules (`module_1`, `module_15`, `module_68`, `module_4`, etc.) based on code analysis?
- **Architectural Pattern Recognition:** Did the agent correctly identify the high-level patterns in use, specifically Event-Driven Architecture and CQRS, citing evidence like separate DB URLs or command/event naming?
- **Data Flow Analysis:** Was the agent's trace of the 'Create Post' flow logical and did it reference the correct sequence of component interactions (API -> Command -> Handler -> Event -> Consumer)?
- **Proposed Solution Viability:** Is the proposed architecture for the whiteboard feature sound? Does it correctly identify WebSockets as the appropriate technology and propose a reasonable strategy for state management and persistence?
- **Visualization Quality:** Are the MermaidJS diagrams syntactically correct, clear, and do they accurately represent both the existing and proposed architectures as described in the analysis?
- **Risk Assessment Insight:** Are the identified risks relevant to the proposed architecture? Does the explanation demonstrate a deep understanding of the trade-offs in distributed, real-time systems (e.g., stateful vs. stateless services, consistency vs. performance)?

60-usertool_resultRead
     1→```rust
     2→//! src/module_50.rs
     3→//!
     4→//! Reliable Domain Event Outbox implementation
     5→//! ===========================================
     6→//! This module provides a production-ready* implementation of the
     7→//! Outbox/Inbox pattern for EduPulse Live.  All domain events are first
     8→//! persisted inside the same Postgres transaction that modified the
     9→//! aggregate and are later *atomically* published to the message broker
    10→//! (e.g. RabbitMQ).  This guarantees *at-least-once* delivery without
    11→//! sacrificing database consistency.
    12→//!
    13→//! # Architecture
    14→//! 1. Domain layer inserts a row into the `outbox_events` table
    15→//!    through [`OutboxRepository::insert`].
    16→//! 2. [`OutboxProcessor`] polls the table on an interval (or is triggered
    17→//!    by NOTIFY/LISTEN) and publishes unpublished events.
    18→//! 3. After a successful publish it marks the event as `published_at`.
    19→//!
    20→//! # Usage
    21→//! ```no_run
    22→//! #[tokio::main]
    23→//! async fn main() -> anyhow::Result<()> {
    24→//!     env_logger::init();
    25→//!
    26→//!     let db = PgPoolOptions::new()
    27→//!         .max_connections(5)
    28→//!         .connect("postgres://user:password@localhost/edupulse")
    29→//!         .await?;
    30→//!
    31→//!     // Initialise AMQP connection
    32→//!     let amqp_addr = "amqp://guest:guest@127.0.0.1:5672/%2f";
    33→//!     let publisher = RabbitMqPublisher::connect(amqp_addr, "edupulse.events").await?;
    34→//!
    35→//!     // Fire-and-forget background processing task
    36→//!     OutboxProcessor::spawn(db.clone(), publisher);
    37→//!
    38→//!     // … start REST API, etc.
    39→//!     Ok(())
    40→//! }
    41→//
... (truncated)

I have completed the comprehensive architectural analysis for the EduPulse Live codebase. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

I analyzed the EduPulse Live event-driven social learning platform to understand its architecture and propose a strategy for integrating a real-time collaborative whiteboard feature.

### Key Architectural Components Identified:

1. **API Gateway** (`module_49`, `module_1`): Actix-Web/Axum-based HTTP routing with JWT middleware
2. **Authentication** (`module_1`): JWT token validation with Redis session store and Argon2 password hashing
3. **Event Publishing** (`module_2`, `module_4`, `module_5`, `module_7`): RabbitMQ (lapin) and NATS (async-nats) publishers
4. **Write Models** (`module_22`, `module_65`): PostgreSQL repositories using sqlx/diesel
5. **Event Consumers** (`module_15`, `module_76`): Badge awarding, search indexing, and other downstream processors
6. **Outbox Processors** (`module_11`, `module_50`, `module_77`): Transactional outbox pattern implementation

### Architectural Patterns:
- **Event-Driven Architecture (EDA)** with strongly-typed domain events
- **CQRS** with separate write (PostgreSQL) and read (Elasticsearch/MeiliSearch) models
- **Transactional Outbox Pattern** for reliable at-least-once event delivery

### Whiteboard Integration Strategy:
- Dedicated WebSocket service using tokio-tungstenite for sub-50ms latency
- Redis Streams for operation buffering and Pub/Sub for cross-instance broadcasting
- Periodic PostgreSQL snapshots for durability
- Integration with existing JWT authentication

### Top 3 Architectural Risks:
1. **WebSocket SPOF**: Stateful servers require sticky sessions and distributed room management
2. **Eventual Consistency**: Whiteboard state may lag behind main platform data
3. **Backpressure**
... (truncated)

Live is an expert-level, event-driven social network for educators and learners that blends course discussions, real-time collaboration, and academic resource sharing.  \nEvery domain concept\u2014lesson publication, quiz submission, peer feedback, badge awards, or payment for premium micro-courses\u2014**emits domain events** that flow through a message broker, keeping the core HTTP API lean and highly responsive.\n\n> TL;DR  \n> `cargo run --package web_social` will spin up the API on <https://localhost:8080>, publish domain events to **RabbitMQ**, persist state in **PostgreSQL**, index resources in **MeiliSearch**, and serve a blazing-fast interactive SPA via **Trunk + Wasm**.\n\n---\n\n## \u2728 Key Capabilities\n\n| Category            | Highlights                                                                              |\n|---------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| Real-time Learning  | \u201cLearning pulses\u201d, live Q&A threads, WebSocket rooms, in-browser code runners           |\n| Event-Driven Core   | Every aggregate action produces a strongly-typed CloudEvent                             |\n| Search & Discovery  | Incremental MeiliSearch indexing via asynchronous workers                               |\n| Achievements        | Badge / XP engine powered by \n* **RabbitMQ 3.12** \u2013 AMQP 0-9-1 event bus  \n* **PostgreSQL 15** \u2013 primary data store, CQRS projections  \n* **MeiliSearch 1.4** \u2013 full-text search  \n* **Redis 7**        \u2013 .arg(user_id.to_string())\n            .arg(\"EX\")\n            .arg(ttl.num_seconds())\n            .query_async(&mut conn)\n            .await?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    #[allow(dead_code)]\n    async fn get_user_id(&self, token: &str) -> anyhow::Result<Option<Uuid>> {\n        let mut conn: Connection = self.pool.get().await?;\n        let resp: Option<String> = conn.get(token).await?;\n        Ok(resp.and_then(|s| Uuid::parse_str(&s).ok()))\n    }\n\n    async fn delete(&self, token: &str) -> anyhow::Result<()> {\n        let mut conn: Connection = self.pool.get().await?;\n        conn.del(token).await?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// =============================================================================================\n/// Service layer\n/// =============================================================================================\npub struct AuthService<R: UserRepository, B: EventBus> {\n    repo: R,\n    event_bus: B,\n    session_store: SessionStore,\n    jwt_secret: String,\n    session_ttl: Duration,\n    argon2: Argon2<'static>,\n}\n\nimpl<R: UserRepository, B: EventBus> AuthService<R, B> {\n    /// Create an [`AuthService`] with sensible defaults.  \n    /// `jwt_secret` **must** be a strong, randomly-generated 256-bit key (base64 encoded).\n    pub fn new(repo: R, event_bus: B, session_store: SessionStore, jwt_secret: String) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            repo,\n            event_bus,\n            session_store,\n            jwt_secret,\n            session_ttl: Duration::hours(12),\n            argon2: Argon2::default(),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Registers a new user, returning a newly minted [`Session`] on success.\n    pub async fn register_user(&self, new_user: NewUser) -> Result<Session> {\n        if self.repo.find_by_email(&new_user.email).await?.is_some() {\n            return Err(AuthError::InvalidCredentials); // simplified: email already taken\n        }\n\n        let salt = SaltString::generate(&mut rand::thread_rng());\n        let password_hash = self\n            .argon2\n            .hash_password(new_user.password.as_bytes(), &salt)?\n            .to_string();\n\n        let user = User {\n            id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n            email: new_user.email,\n            password_hash,\n            created_at: Utc::now(),\n        };\n\n        self.repo.insert(&user).await?;\n        self.event_bus\n            .publish(&DomainEvent::UserRegistered {\n                user_id: user.id,\n                email: user.email.clone(),\n            })\n            .await?;\n\n        let session = self.create_session(user.id).await?;\n        Ok(session)\n    }\n\n    /// Authenticates a user and returns a valid session token.\n    pub async fn login_user(&self, email: &str, password: &str) -> Result<Session> {\n        let user = self\n            .repo\n            .find_by_email(email)\n            .await?\n            .ok_or(AuthError::InvalidCredentials)?;\n\n        // Verify password\n        let parsed_hash = PasswordHash::new(&user.password_hash)?;\n        self.argon2\n            .verify_password(password.as_bytes(), &parsed_hash)\n            .map_err(|_| AuthError::InvalidCredentials)?;\n\n        let session = self.create_session(user.id).await?;\n\n        self.event_bus\n            .publish(&DomainEvent::UserLoggedIn { user_id: user.id })\n            .await?;\n\n        Ok(session)\n    }\n\n    /// Invalidates an existing session.\n    pub async fn logout_user(&self, token: &str) -> Result<()> {\n        self.session_store\n            .delete(token)\n            .await\n            .map_err(|e| AuthError::EventBus(e.into()))?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Helper: create a JWT token + Redis cache entry.\n    async fn create_session(&self, user_id: Uuid) -> Result<Session> {\n        let now = Utc::now();\n        let exp = (now + self.session_ttl).timestamp() as usize;\n\n        let claims = Claims {\n            sub: user_id.to_string(),\n            exp,\n            iat: now.timestamp() as usize,\n        };\n\n        let header = Header::default();\n        let token = encode(\n            &header,\n            &claims,\n            &EncodingKey::from_secret(self.jwt_secret.as_bytes()),\n        )?;\n\n        // Cache in Redis for server-side revocation\n        self.session_store\n            .put(&token, user_id, self.session_ttl)\n            .await\n            .map_err(|e| AuthError::EventBus(e.into()))?;\n\n        Ok(Session {\n            token,\n            expires_at: now + self.session_ttl,\n        })\n    }\n\n    /// Validate a token and return the user id embedded in it.\n    pub async fn validate_token(&self, token: &str) -> Result<Uuid> {\n        // 1. Verify signature / expiration\n        let TokenData { claims, .. } = decode::<Claims>(\n            token,\n            &DecodingKey::from_secret(self.jwt_secret.as_bytes()),\n            &Validation::default(),\n        )?;\n\n        // 2. Check server-side revocation list (Redis)\n        if self\n            .session_store\n            .get_user_id(token)\n            .await\n            .map_err(|e| AuthError::EventBus(e.into()))?\n            .is_none()\n        {\n            return Err(AuthError::InvalidCredentials);\n        }\n\n        let uuid = Uuid::parse_str(&claims.sub).map_err(|_| AuthError::InvalidCredentials)?;\n        Ok(uuid)\n    }\n}\n\n/// =============================================================================================\n/// REST handler glue (simplified for brevity). In a real project, this would live in actix-web or\n/// axum route modules. Here we show just enough to demonstrate SVC integration.\n/// =============================================================================================\n#[cfg(feature = \"rest_api\")]\npub mod rest {\n    use super::*;\n    use axum::{\n        extract::{Extension, Json},\n        http::StatusCode,\n        response::IntoResponse,\n        routing::post,\n        Router,\n    };\n    use std::sync::Arc;\n\n    #[derive(Clone)]\n    pub struct AppState<A> {\n        pub auth_service: Arc<A>,\n    }\n\n    pub fn router<A: 'static + Send + Sync>(\n        state: AppState<A>,\n    ) -> Router\n    where\n        A: AuthServiceTrait,\n    {\n        Router::new()\n            .route(\"/api/v1/auth/register\", post(register::<A>))\n            .route(\"/api/v1/auth/login\", post(login::<A>))\n            .layer(Extension(state))\n    }\n\n    #[async_trait]\n    pub trait AuthServiceTrait: Send + Sync {\n        async fn register(&self, new_user: NewUser) -> Result<Session>;\n        async fn login(&self, email: &str, password: &str) -> Result<Session>;\n    }\n\n    #[async_trait]\n    impl<R, B> AuthServiceTrait for super::AuthService<R, B>\n    where\n        R: UserRepository + 'static,\n        B: EventBus + 'static,\n    {\n        async fn register(&self, new_user: NewUser) -> Result<Session> {\n            self.register_user(new_user).await\n        }\n\n        async fn login(&self, email: &str, password: &str) -> Result<Session> {\n            self.login_user(email, password).await\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Extension(state): Extension<AppState<A>>,\n    ) -> impl IntoResponse\n    where\n        A: AuthServiceTrait,\n    {\n        match state.auth_service.register(payload).await {\n            Ok(session) => (StatusCode::CREATED, Json(session)).into_response(),\n            Err(e) => {\n                error!(\"registration error: {e}\");\n                (StatusCode::BAD_REQUEST, Json(e.to_string())).into_response()\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[derive(Deserialize)]\n    struct LoginPayload {\n        email: String,\n        password: String,\n    }\n\n    async fn login<A>(\n        Json(payload): Json<LoginPayload>,\n        Extension(state): Extension<AppState<A>>,\n    ) -> impl IntoResponse\n    where\n        A: AuthServiceTrait,\n    {\n        match         Err(e) => {\n                error!(\"login error: {e}\");\n                (StatusCode::UNAUTHORIZED, Json(e.to_string())).into_response()\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// random key)\");\n\n    let pool = PgPool::connect(&database_url).await?;\n\n    let repo = PostgresUserRepository::new(pool);\n    let bus = TracingEventBus;\n    let session_store = This module materialises the *Domain Event* concept mentioned in the\n//! architecture description and provides a pluggable, async publisher that can\n//! be wired to a real message-broker (e.g. RabbitMQ via *lapin*) or gracefully\n//! degrade to a pure in-process logger in tests or local development.\n//!\n//! Key design points\n//! -----------------\n//! \u2022 A strongly-typed `DomainEvent` enum prevents the *stringly-typed* antipattern.  \n//! \u2022 An `EventEnvelope` carries universal metadata used by downstream services.  \n//! \u2022 The `EventPublisher` trait abstracts the transport; a concrete\n//!   `RabbitMqPublisher` is behind a crate feature flag (`broker`).  \n//! \u2022 `thiserror` provides ergonomic error handling.  \n//! \u2022 `async_trait` allows `async` functions in traits while staying on stable Rust.\n//!\n//! -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n//! Crate features\n//! --------------\n//! `broker` \u2013 Enables the real AMQP publisher that talks to RabbitMQ.  When the\n//! feature is **not** enabled, a lightweight logger implementation is compiled\n//! instead.  fn default() -> Self {\n        Self {\n            id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n            occurred_at: Utc::now(),\n            source: env!(\"CARGO_PKG_NAME\").to_owned(),\n            correlation_id: Each variant is versioned so we can evolve payloads\n/// without breaking existing subscribers.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n#[serde(tag = \"type\", content = \"payload\")]\npub enum DomainEvent {\n    /// A teacher has published a new lesson.\n    LessonPublishedV1 {\n        lesson_id: Uuid,\n        title: String,\n        author_id: Uuid,\n    },\n\n    /// A student submitted answers to a quiz.\n    QuizSubmittedV1 {\n        quiz_id: Uuid,\n        attempt_id: Uuid,\n        student_id: Uuid,\n    },\n\n    /// A peer gave feedback to someone else's submission.\n    PeerFeedbackGivenV1 {\n        feedback_id: Uuid,\n        submission_id: Uuid,\n        reviewer_id: Uuid,\n    },\n\n    /// A student was granted a badge.\n    BadgeAwardedV1 {\n        badge_id: Uuid,\n        awardee_id: Uuid,\n        reason: String,\n    },\n\n    /// Money changed hands for a premium micro-course.\n    PaymentCapturedV1 {\n        payment_id: Uuid,\n        amount_cents: i64,\n        currency: String,\n        payer_id: Uuid,\n    },\n}\n\n/// Envelope that wraps the event payload with universal metadata.\n///\n/// Storing metadata *outside* the payload makes it trivial to evolve individual\n/// events without duplicating the same bookkeeping fields everywhere.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct EventEnvelope {\n    pub meta: EventMetadata,\n    pub event: DomainEvent,\n}\n\nimpl EventEnvelope {\n    pub fn new<E: Into<DomainEvent>>(event: E) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            meta: EventMetadata::default(),\n            event: event.into(),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Serialise the envelope into a compact JSON payload.\n///\n/// We purposefully avoid pretty printing for network efficiency; producers that\n/// want human-readable output can call `pretty_json()` instead.\nimpl EventEnvelope {\n    pub fn to_json_bytes(&self) -> Result<Vec<u8>, EventError> {\n        Ok(serde_json::to_vec(self)?)\n    }\n\n    #[allow(dead_code)]\n    pub fn pretty_json(&self) -> Result<String, EventError> {\n        Ok(serde_json::to_string_pretty(self)?)\n    }\n\n    /// Derive the *logical* routing key used in AMQP brokers.  Topic exchange\n    /// policies can fan-out events to multiple queues, e.g. `lesson.published.v1`.\n    pub fn routing_key(&self) -> String {\n        match &self.event {\n            DomainEvent::LessonPublishedV1 { .. } => \"lesson.published.v1\",\n            DomainEvent::QuizSubmittedV1 { .. } => \"quiz.submitted.v1\",\n            DomainEvent::PeerFeedbackGivenV1 { .. } => \"feedback.given.v1\",\n            DomainEvent::BadgeAwardedV1 { .. } => \"badge.awarded.v1\",\n            DomainEvent::PaymentCapturedV1 { .. } => \"payment.captured.v1\",\n        }\n        .into()\n    }\n}\n\n/// Error type for publishing and serialisation failures.\n#[derive(Error, Debug)]\npub enum EventError {\n    #[error(\"serialization error: {0}\")]\n    Serialization(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n\n    #[cfg(feature = \"broker\")]\n    #[error(\"amqp error: {0}\")]\n    Amqp(#[from] lapin::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"broker confirmation timed out\")]\n    ConfirmationTimeout,\n\n    #[error(\"other: {0}\")]\n    Other(String),\n}\n\n/// Trait every publisher (mock or real) must implement.\n///\n/// The abstraction enables dependency injection in application services and\n/// makes *unit* testing simpler:  we can just inject the `LoggingPublisher`.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait EventPublisher: Send + Sync {\n    async fn publish(&self, envelope: EventEnvelope) -> Result<(), EventError>;\n}\n\n/// A publisher that merely writes events to the `log` sink.\n///\n/// Enabled by default, also used when the `broker` feature is disabled. The\n/// design means the rest of the application can always depend on\n/// `dyn EventPublisher`, regardless of compilation mode.\npub struct LoggingPublisher;\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl EventPublisher for LoggingPublisher {\n    async fn publish(&self, envelope: EventEnvelope) -> Result<(), EventError> {\n        // Format into single-line JSON to keep log ingestion systems happy.\n        let json = envelope.to_json_bytes()?;\n        // Safe because JSON is UTF-8.\n        log::info!(\n            target: \"eduplse.events\",\n            \"event={} meta_id={} payload={}\",\n            envelope.routing_key(),\n            envelope.meta.id,\n            String::from_utf8_lossy(&json)\n        );\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// Real AMQP publisher that talks to RabbitMQ.  \n///\n/// Compiled **only** when the `broker` feature is present.  Uses publisher\n/// confirms so we know the broker durably persisted the message.\n#[cfg(feature = \"broker\")]\npub struct RabbitMqPublisher {\n    channel: Channel,\n    exchange: String,\n}\n\n#[cfg(feature = \"broker\")]\nimpl RabbitMqPublisher {\n    /// Connect to the AMQP broker and prepare the channel.\n    ///\n    /// A production-grade implementation would configure TLS, heartbeat, and\n    /// automatic reconnection. Those details are omitted for brevity.\n    pub async fn connect(\n        amqp_uri: &str,\n        exchange: &str,\n    ) -> Result<Self, EventError> {\n        let connection = Connection::connect(\n            amqp_uri,\n            ConnectionProperties::default().with_default_executor(8),\n        )\n        .await\n        .map_err(EventError::from)?;\n\n        let channel = connection.create_channel().await?;\n        channel\n            .confirm_select(lapin::options::ConfirmSelectOptions::default())\n            .await?;\n\n        Ok(Self {\n            channel,\n            exchange: exchange.to_owned(),\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n#[cfg(feature = \"broker\")]\n#[async_trait]\nimpl EventPublisher for RabbitMqPublisher {\n    async fn publish(&self, envelope: EventEnvelope) -> Result<(), EventError> {\n        let payload = envelope.to_json_bytes()?;\n        let routing_key = envelope.routing_key();\n\n        let confirm: Confirmation = self\n            .channel\n            .basic_publish(\n                &self.exchange,\n                &routing_key,\n                BasicPublishOptions {\n                    mandatory: false,\n                    immediate: false,\n                },\n                &payload,\n                BasicProperties::default().with_content_type(\"application/json\"),\n            )\n            .await?\n            .await?; // Wait for broker confirm (publisher confirms must be enabled)\n\n        // lapin returns Nack(\u2026) in error path; we check for `Ack`.\n        if !confirm.is_ack() {\n            return Err(EventError::Other(format!(\n                \"broker did not acknowledge event id {}\",\n                envelope.meta.id\n            )));\n        }\n\n        // Additionally enforce a #[error(\"connection pool exhausted\")]\n    PoolTimeout(#[from] r2d2::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"serialization error: {0}\")]\n    Serde(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"message broker self.pool.get().map_err(AppError::PoolTimeout)\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait::async_trait]\nimpl LearningPulseRepository for DieselLearningPulseRepo {\n    async fn insert(&self, pulse: LearningPulse) -> .values(&new_pulse)\n                .execute(&conn)\n        })\n        .await\n        .expect(\"spawn_blocking panicked\")?; // propagate diesel::Error\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    async fn learning_pulses::table\n                .find(id)\n                .first(&conn)\n                .optional()\n        })\n        .await\n        .expect(\"spawn_blocking panicked\")?;\n        Ok(result)\n    }\n\n    async fn list_recent(&self, limit: i64) -> Result<Vec<LearningPulse>, AppError> {\n        let conn = self.conn()?;\n        let pulses = tokio::task::spawn_blocking(move || {\n            learning_pulses::table\n                .order(learning_pulses::created_at.desc())\n                .limit(limit)\n                .load::<LearningPulse>(&conn)\n        })\n        .await\n        .expect(\"spawn_blocking panicked\")?;\n        Ok(pulses)\n    }\n}\n\n/// Abstraction over any message broker that can deliver domain events.\n#[async_trait::async_trait]\npub trait NatsPublisher {\n    pub async fn connect_from_env() -> Result<Self, AppError> {\n        let nats_url = std::env::var(\"NATS_URL\").unwrap_or_else(|_| \"nats://127.0.0.1:4222\".into());\n        let }\n}\n\n#[async_trait::async_trait]\nimpl EventPublisher for NatsPublisher {\n    async fn publish(&self, ev: &DomainEvent) -> Result<(), AppError> {\n        let subject = self.subject_for(ev);\n LearningPulseService {\n    pub fn new(\n        repo: Arc<dyn LearningPulseRepository>,\n        publisher: Arc<dyn EventPublisher>,\n    ) -> Self {\n        let (tx, mut rx) = mpsc::channel::<DomainEvent>(1024);\n        let publisher_clone = publisher.clone();\n\n        // Spawn background task to forward events.\n        tokio::spawn(async move {\n            while let Some(ev) = rx.recv().await {\n                if let Err(e) = publisher_clone.publish(&ev).await {\n                    // TODO: push to dead-letter queue or retry mechanism.\n    teacher_id,\n            title,\n            body,\n            tags,\n            created_at: now,\n            updated_at: now,\n        };\n\n        // --- Persistence .connection_timeout(std::time::Duration::from_secs(5))\n        .build(manager)?;\n\n    let repo = Arc::new(DieselLearningPulseRepo::new(pool));\n    let publisher = This module defines strongly-typed domain events, an event envelope,\n//! trait abstractions for publishers/consumers, and a RabbitMQ publisher\n//! implementation using the `lapin` crate.  It demonstrates how the core\n//! service layer can remain broker-agnostic while individual adapters\n//! implement the I/O details behind the trait objects.\n//!\n//! The code purposefully favours composition over inheritance and\n//! separates business-level concerns from transport-level concerns,\n//! adhering to the Dependency-Inversion Principle.\n//!\n//! # Dependencies\n//!\n//! Add the following to `Cargo.toml` (omitting unrelated project deps):\n//!\n//! ```toml\n//! All domain\n//! models raise strongly-typed events that are wrapped in an `EventEnvelope`\n//! and forwarded to a message broker (e.g. NATS, Kafka) so that downstream\n//! services can react asynchronously (scoring, analytics, notifications, \u2026).\n//!\n//! Compile-time feature flags\n//! \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\n//! \u2502 default      = [\"memory\"]\n//! \u2502 \"nats\"       = enable NATS-backed publisher/subscriber\n//! \u2502 \"memory\"     = enable in-memory publisher/subscriber (tests & dev)\n//! \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\n//! Note: add the corresponding optional dependencies to `Cargo.toml`\n//!\n//!     async-nats = { version = \"0.32\", optional = true, features = [\"tls\"] }\n//!     tokio      = { version = \"1.36\", features = [\"full\"] }\n//!     serde      = { version = \"1.0\",  features = [\"derive\"] }\n//!     async-trait= \"0.1\"\n//!     uuid       = { version = \"1.7\",  features = [\"serde\", \"v4\"] }\n//!     chrono     = { version = \"0.4\",  features = [\"serde\"] }\n//!     tracing    = \"0.1\"\n//!     thiserror  = \"1.0\"\n//!\n\nuse std::fmt::Debug;\n\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse serde::{de::DeserializeOwned, Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse thiserror::Error;\nuse tracing::{debug, error, info, warn};\nuse uuid::Uuid;\n\n/// Common failure modes that can occur when publishing or handling events.\n#[derive(Error, Debug)]\npub enum EventBusError {\n    #[error(\"serialization error: {0}\")]\n    Serialization(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n\n    #[cfg(feature = \"nats\")]\n    #[error(\"NATS error: {0}\")]\n    Nats(#[from] async_nats::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"channel send error: {0}\")]\n    ChannelSend(String),\n\n    #[error(\"handler error: {0}\")]\n    Handler(String),\n}\n\n/// A domain event encapsulates something that occurred within a bounded context.\n///\n/// It must be cheap to copy (hence `Clone`) and serializable (`Serialize`, `DeserializeOwned`).\npub trait DomainEvent: Debug + Clone + Serialize + DeserializeOwned + Send + Sync + 'static {\n    /// Globally unique event name, e.g. `\"LearningPulseCreated\"`.\n    fn event_type() -> &'static str;\n}\n\n/// Envelope that adds cross-cutting metadata (id, timestamp) to an event.\n///\n/// This is the actual payload sent across the wire.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct EventEnvelope<E: DomainEvent> {\n    pub id:            Uuid,\n    pub occurred_at:   DateTime<Utc>,\n    pub aggregate_id:  Uuid,\n    pub payload:       E,\n}\n\nimpl<E: DomainEvent> EventEnvelope<E> {\n    pub fn new(aggregate_id: Uuid, payload: E) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n            occurred_at: Utc::now(),\n            aggregate_id,\n            payload,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the subject / topic name that should be used when publishing the event.\n    pub fn subject(&self) -> String {\n        format!(\"edu.{}\", E::event_type())\n    }\n}\n\n/// Publish-only half of the event bus.\n///\n/// Services emitting events depend only on `EventPublisher`.  They do not care\n/// about how the events are shipped (NATS, Kafka, in-memory).\n#[async_trait]\npub trait EventPublisher: Send + Sync {\n    async fn publish<E: DomainEvent>(&self, envelope: EventEnvelope<E>) -> Result<(), EventBusError>;\n}\n\n/// Subscribe-side abstraction that allows registering strongly-typed handlers.\n///\n/// A handler can be any async function that takes the deserialized envelope.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait EventSubscriber: Send + Sync {\n    async fn subscribe<E, F>(&self, handler: F) -> Result<(), EventBusError>\n    where\n        E: DomainEvent,\n        F: Fn(EventEnvelope<E>) -> futures::future::BoxFuture<'static, Result<(), EventBusError>>\n            + Send\n            + Sync\n            + 'static;\n}\n\n////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n/// In-memory reference implementation (dev / tests)\n////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n#[cfg(feature = \"memory\")]\npub mod memory {\n    use super::*;\n    use futures::{future::BoxFuture, FutureExt};\n    use std::collections::HashMap;\n    use tokio::sync::broadcast;\n\n    type DynSender = broadcast::Sender<Vec<u8>>;\n\n    /// Simple bus built on `tokio::broadcast`. Great for unit tests.\n    #[derive(Clone, Default)]\n    pub struct InMemoryBus {\n        channels: std::sync::Arc<tokio::sync::Mutex<HashMap<&'static str, DynSender>>>,\n    }\n\n    impl InMemoryBus {\n        async fn get_sender(&self, topic: &'static str) -> DynSender {\n            let mut map = self.channels.lock().await;\n            map.entry(topic)\n                .or_insert_with(|| broadcast::channel::<Vec<u8>>(1024).0)\n                .clone()\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[async_trait]\n    impl EventPublisher for InMemoryBus {\n        async fn publish<E: DomainEvent>(\n            &self,\n            envelope: EventEnvelope<E>,\n        ) -> Result<(), EventBusError> {\n            let bytes = serde_json::to_vec(&envelope)?;\n            let sender = self.get_sender(E::event_type()).await;\n            sender\n                .send(bytes)\n                .map_err(|e| EventBusError::ChannelSend(e.to_string()))?;\n            debug!(\n                \"InMemoryBus published event {} ({})\",\n                E::event_type(),\n                envelope.id\n            );\n            Ok(())\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[async_trait]\n    impl EventSubscriber for InMemoryBus {\n        async fn subscribe<E, F>(&self, handler: F) -> Result<(), EventBusError>\n        where\n            E: DomainEvent,\n            F: Fn(EventEnvelope<E>) -> BoxFuture<'static, Result<(), EventBusError>>\n                + Send\n                + Sync\n                + 'static,\n        {\n            let receiver = self.get_sender(E::event_type()).await.subscribe();\n\n            tokio::spawn(async move {\n                let mut rx = receiver;\n                while let Ok(bytes) = rx.recv().await {\n                    match serde_json::from_slice::<EventEnvelope<E>>(&bytes) {\n                        Ok(env) => {\n                            if let Err(err) = handler(env).await {\n                                error!(\"event handler failed: {}\", err);\n                            }\n                        }\n                        Err(err) => error!(\"failed to deserialize event: {}\", err),\n                    }\n                }\n            });\n\n            Ok(())\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n/// NATS implementation (production)\n////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n#[cfg(feature = \"nats\")]\npub mod nats {\n    use super::*;\n    use async_nats::{ConnectOptions, Connection, Subscriber};\n    use futures::{future::BoxFuture, StreamExt};\n    use std::sync::Arc;\n\n    /// NATS-based pub/sub using JSON payloads.\n    #[derive(Clone)]\n    pub struct NatsBus {\n        connection: Arc<Connection>,\n        subject_prefix: String,\n    }\n\n    impl NatsBus {\n        /// Establish a TLS-enabled NATS connection.  Supply a comma-separated list\n        /// of servers (e.g. `\"nats://localhost:4222,nats://backup:4222\"`).\n        pub async fn new(servers: &str, subject_prefix: impl Into<String>) -> Result<Self, EventBusError> {\n            let conn = ConnectOptions::new()\n                .require_tls(true)\n                .connect(servers)\n                .await?;\n            Ok(Self {\n                connection: Arc::new(conn),\n                subject_prefix: subject_prefix.into(),\n            })\n        }\n\n        fn compose_subject<E: DomainEvent>(&self) -> String {\n            format!(\"{}.{}\", self.subject_prefix, E::event_type())\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[async_trait]\n    impl EventPublisher for NatsBus {\n        async fn publish<E: DomainEvent>(\n            &self,\n            envelope: EventEnvelope<E>,\n        ) -> Result<(), EventBusError> {\n            let subject = self.compose_subject::<E>();\n            let data = serde_json::to_vec(&envelope)?;\n            self.connection.publish(subject.clone(), data.into()).await?;\n            info!(\n                \"NatsBus published event {} on '{}'\",\n                envelope.id, subject\n            );\n            Ok(())\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[async_trait]\n    impl EventSubscriber for NatsBus {\n        async fn subscribe<E, F>(&self, handler: F) -> Result<(), EventBusError>\n        where\n            E: DomainEvent,\n            F: Fn(EventEnvelope<E>) -> BoxFuture<'static, Result<(), EventBusError>>\n                + Send\n                + Sync\n                + 'static,\n        {\n            let subject = self.compose_subject::<E>();\n            let sub: Subscriber = self.connection.subscribe(subject.clone()).await?;\n            info!(\"NatsBus subscribed to '{}'\", subject);\n\n            tokio::spawn(async move {\n                let mut stream = sub;\n                while let Some(msg) = stream.next().await {\n                    if let Ok(env) = serde_json::from_slice::<EventEnvelope<E>>(&msg.payload) {\n                        if let Err(err) = handler(env).await {\n                            error!(\"handler error: {}\", err);\n Error)]\npub enum BrokerError {\n    #[error(\"message serialization failed: {0}\")]\n    Serialization(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"channel error: {0}\")]\n    Channel(#[from]    /// Optional correlation id to track causality chains.\n    #[serde(skip_serializing_if = \"Option::is_none\")]\n    pub correlation_id: Option<Uuid>,\n\n    /// Actual domain payload.\n    pub payload: T,\n}\n\nimpl<T> EventEnvelope<T>\nwhere\n    T: Serialize + Send + Sync + 'static,\n{\n    /// Create a new envelope with the current system time.\n    pub fn new(topic: impl Into<Topic>,         .expect(\"system clock drift\")\n                .as_millis(),\n            correlation_id: None,\n            payload,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Attach or overwrite the correlation id.\n T: Serialize + Send + Sync + 'static;\n\n    /// Subscribe to a topic, returning a stream-like handle.\n    async fn subscribe(&self, topic: Topic) -> Result<Subscription, BrokerError>;\n\n    /// &self.topic\n    }\n\n    pub async fn recv(&mut self) -> Result<Vec<u8>, BrokerError> {\n        let bytes = self.rx.recv().await?;\n        Ok(bytes)\n    }\n}\n\n/// In-memory broker backed by broadcast::channel::<Vec<u8>>(1024).0)\n            .clone()\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl EventBroker for InMemoryBroker {\n    async fn publish<T>(&self, event: EventEnvelope<T>) -> Result<(), Err(BrokerError::Unknown(e.to_string()))\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    async fn subscribe(&self, topic: Topic) -> Result<Subscription, BrokerError> {\n        let sender = self.get_sender(&topic).await;\n        Ok(Subscription {\n            topic,\n            rx: sender.subscribe(),\n        })\n    }\n\n    async fn stop(&self) -> Result<(), BrokerError> {\n        let mut tasks = self.tasks.lock().await;\n        for handle in tasks.drain(..) {\n            handle.abort();\n        }\n        info!(\"in-memory broker stopped\");\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// Example domain events.\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct LessonPublished {\n    pub lesson_id: Uuid,\n    pub author_id: Uuid,\n    pub title: String,\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct QuizSubmitted {\n    pub quiz_id: Uuid,\n    pub student_id: Uuid,\n    pub score: f32,\n}\n\n/// High-level typed facade used Ok(TypedSubscription::from_raw(raw))\n    }\n\n    pub async fn on_quiz_submitted(\n        &self,\n    ) -> Result<TypedSubscription<QuizSubmitted>, BrokerError> {\n        let raw = An event\u2013driven badge\u2013awarding micro-service for the\n//! \u201cEduPulse Live \u2013 Event-Driven Social Learning Hub\u201d platform.\n//!\n//! This module demonstrates how the core application publishes\n//! domain events while an out-of-process, autonomous component\n//! (here: `BadgeAwardService`) consumes them, performs business\n//! logic, persists the result and publishes its own follow-up\n//! events.  \n//!\n//! The service is completely self-contained: it hosts an in-memory\n//! dispatcher for local development, yet persists events and state\n//! in Postgres so it can be moved into a distributed setting\n//! later on (e.g. with NATS/Kafka\u2010backed `Dispatcher`).\n//!\n//! Architectural patterns shown here:\n//!   \u2022 Repository Pattern      \u2013 decoupling persistence\n//!   \u2022 Service Layer           \u2013 `BadgeAwardService`\n//!   \u2022 Event Sourcing          \u2013 immutable `EventStore`\n//!   \u2022 Async Rust w/ Tokio     \u2013 non-blocking I/O\n//!   \u2022 Error Handling w/ thiserror + anyhow\n//!\n//! NOTE: In a real-world project this module would be split\n//! into several files/crates.  Everything is co-located here only\n//! to satisfy the single-file constraint of the exercise.\n\nuse std::{\n    collections::HashSet,\n    sync::Arc,\n    time::Duration,\n};\n\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse sqlx::{postgres::PgPoolOptions, PgPool};\nuse thiserror::Error;\nuse tokio::{\n    select,\n    sync::{broadcast, mpsc, RwLock},\n    task::JoinHandle,\n};\nuse uuid::Uuid;\n\n/// Domain events which can be emitted by EduPulse services.\n///\n/// IMPORTANT: New variants **must** implement `Serialize`/`Deserialize`\n/// so they can be persisted in the event store.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n#[serde(tag = \"type\", content = \"payload\")]\npub enum DomainEvent {\n    QuizSubmitted(QuizSubmitted),\n    BadgeAwarded(BadgeAwarded),\n    // \u2026 more variants omitted for brevity\n}\n\nimpl DomainEvent {\n    /// Helper returning event name for logging / metrics.\n    pub fn name(&self) -> &'static str {\n        match self {\n            DomainEvent::QuizSubmitted(_) => \"QuizSubmitted\",\n            DomainEvent::BadgeAwarded(_) => \"BadgeAwarded\",\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Metadata common to all envelopes\u2014separates immutable event data\n/// from peripheral transport concerns such as IDs and timestamps.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct EventEnvelope {\n    pub id: Uuid,\n    pub occurred_at: DateTime<Utc>,\n    pub event: DomainEvent,\n}\n\nimpl EventEnvelope {\n    pub fn new(event: DomainEvent) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n            occurred_at: Utc::now(),\n            event,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Event data triggered when a learner submits a quiz.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct QuizSubmitted {\n    pub quiz_id: Uuid,\n    pub learner_id: Uuid,\n    pub score: f32,\n}\n\n/// Event data emitted once the learner qualifies for a badge.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct BadgeAwarded {\n    pub badge_id: Uuid,\n    pub learner_id: Uuid,\n    pub awarded_at: DateTime<Utc>,\n    pub reason: String,\n}\n\n/// Central event dispatcher.  \n/// Internally uses a Tokio broadcast channel so any number of\n/// in-process consumers can receive events concurrently.\n///\n/// In production you might replace the implementation with NATS,\n/// Kafka, RabbitMQ\u2026 etc., leaving the public API intact.\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct Dispatcher {\n    sender: broadcast::Sender<EventEnvelope>,\n}\n\nimpl Dispatcher {\n    /// Create a new dispatcher with a configurable ring buffer size.\n    pub fn new(channel_size: usize) -> Self {\n        let (sender, _rx) = broadcast::channel(channel_size);\n        Self { sender }\n    }\n\n    /// Publish an envelope to all subscribers.\n    pub async fn publish(&self, envelope: EventEnvelope) {\n        // broadcast::Sender::send is synchronous but inexpensive.\n        // Failure only occurs when there are no active receivers;\n        // still, we ignore that because the event is persisted in\n        // the store before reaching this point.\n        let _ = self.sender.send(envelope);\n    }\n\n    /// Subscribe to a continuous stream of events.\n    pub fn subscribe(&self) -> broadcast::Receiver<EventEnvelope> {\n        self.sender.subscribe()\n    }\n}\n\n/// Persisted event stream; provides idempotent append + read access.\n/// Uses Postgres JSONB for flexible schema evolution.\n///\n/// Table DDL (run via migrations):\n/// ```sql\n/// CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS event_store (\n///     id           UUID PRIMARY KEY,\n///     occurred_at  TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE NOT NULL,\n///     event_name   TEXT NOT NULL,\n///     payload      JSONB NOT NULL\n/// );\n/// ```\npub struct EventStore {\n    pool: PgPool,\n}\n\nimpl EventStore {\n    pub async fn new(db_url: &str, max_connections: u32) -> Result<Self, sqlx::Error> {\n        let pool = PgPoolOptions::new()\n            .max_connections(max_connections)\n            .connect(db_url)\n            .await?;\n        Ok(Self { pool })\n    }\n\n    /// Append envelope to store.\n    pub async fn append(&self, env: &EventEnvelope) -> Result<(), sqlx::Error> {\n        sqlx::query!(\n            r#\"\n            INSERT INTO event_store (id, occurred_at, event_name, payload)\n            VALUES ($1, $2, $3, $4)\n            \"#,\n            env.id,\n            env.occurred_at,\n            env.event.name(),\n            serde_json::to_value(&env.event)?\n        )\n        .execute(&self.pool)\n        .await?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Read events by name\u2014useful for rebuilding read models.\n    pub async fn load_by_event(\n        &self,\n        event_name: &str,\n    ) -> Result<Vec<EventEnvelope>, sqlx::Error> {\n        let recs = sqlx::query!(\n            r#\"\n            SELECT id, occurred_at, payload\n            FROM event_store\n            WHERE event_name = $1\n            ORDER BY occurred_at ASC\n            \"#,\n            event_name\n        )\n        .fetch_all(&self.pool)\n        .await?;\n\n        recs.into_iter()\n            .map(|r| {\n                let event = match event_name {\n                    \"QuizSubmitted\" => DomainEvent::QuizSubmitted(\n                        serde_json::from_value(r.payload)?,\n                    ),\n                    \"BadgeAwarded\" => DomainEvent::BadgeAwarded(\n                        serde_json::from_value(r.payload)?,\n                    ),\n                    _ => unreachable!(\"Unknown event stored in DB\"),\n                };\n                Ok(EventEnvelope {\n                    id: r.id,\n                    occurred_at: r.occurred_at,\n                    event,\n                })\n            })\n            .collect()\n    }\n}\n\n/// Error type covering all repository/service error cases.\n#[derive(Error, Debug)]\npub enum ServiceError {\n    #[error(\"Database error: {0}\")]\n    Database(#[from] sqlx::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"Event serialisation error: {0}\")]\n    Serde(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"Internal channel closed\")]\n    ChannelClosed,\n}\n\n/// Repository abstraction for badge persistence.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait BadgeRepository: Send + Sync {\n    async fn learner_already_has_badge(\n        &self,\n        learner_id: Uuid,\n        badge_id: Uuid,\n    ) -> Result<bool, ServiceError>;\n\n    async fn assign_badge(\n        &self,\n        learner_id: Uuid,\n        badge: &BadgeAwarded,\n    ) -> Result<(), ServiceError>;\n}\n\n/// Postgres-based implementation of the `BadgeRepository`.\n///\n/// Table DDL:\n/// ```sql\n/// CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS learner_badges (\n///     learner_id UUID NOT NULL,\n///     badge_id   UUID NOT NULL,\n///     awarded_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE NOT NULL,\n///     reason     TEXT NOT NULL,\n///     PRIMARY KEY (learner_id, badge_id)\n/// );\n/// ```\npub struct PgBadgeRepository {\n    pool: PgPool,\n}\n\nimpl PgBadgeRepository {\n    pub fn new(pool: PgPool) -> Self {\n        Self { pool }\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl BadgeRepository for PgBadgeRepository {\n    async fn learner_already_has_badge(\n        &self,\n        learner_id: Uuid,\n        badge_id: Uuid,\n    ) -> Result<bool, ServiceError> {\n        let res = sqlx::query_scalar!(\n            r#\"\n            SELECT EXISTS (\n                SELECT 1\n                FROM learner_badges\n                WHERE learner_id = $1 AND badge_id = $2\n            ) AS \"exists!\"\n            \"#,\n            learner_id,\n            badge_id\n        )\n        .fetch_one(&self.pool)\n        .await?;\n\n        Ok(res.unwrap_or(false))\n    }\n\n    async fn assign_badge(\n        &self,\n        learner_id: Uuid,\n        badge: &BadgeAwarded,\n    ) -> Result<(), ServiceError> {\n        sqlx::query!(\n            r#\"\n            INSERT INTO learner_badges (learner_id, badge_id, awarded_at, reason)\n            VALUES ($1, $2, $3, $4)\n            \"#,\n            learner_id,\n            badge.badge_id,\n            badge.awarded_at,\n            badge.reason\n        )\n        .execute(&self.pool)\n        .await?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// Business logic deciding whether a quiz submission qualifies\n/// for a badge.  Runs fully asynchronously, keeping its own\n/// subscription to the dispatcher.\n///\n/// Scoring rules used here are intentionally simple:  \n/// \u2013 Score \u2265 90 %      \u21d2 \u201cQuiz Master\u201d badge (UUID hard-coded)  \n/// \u2013 Score exactly 100 \u21d2 special \u201cPerfect Score\u201d badge\npub struct BadgeAwardService<R: BadgeRepository + 'static> {\n    repo: Arc<R>,\n Arc<R>,\n        dispatcher: Dispatcher,\n        event_store: Arc<EventStore>,\n    ) -> Self {\n        // Hard-coded UUIDs of known badges.\n        let subscribed_badges = vec![\n            // \u201cQuiz Master\u201d\n            Uuid::parse_str(\"11111111-1111-1111-1111-111111111111\").unwrap(),\n            // \u201cPerfect Score\u201d\n            Uuid::parse_str(\"22222222-2222-2222-2222-222222222222\").unwrap(),\n        ]\n        .into_iter()\n        .collect();\n\n        Self {\n            repo,\n            dispatcher,\n            event_store,\n            subscribed_badges,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Spawn the service on the Tokio runtime; returns its `JoinHandle`\n    /// so callers can `.await` graceful shutdown.\n    pub fn spawn(self: Arc<Self>) -> JoinHandle<()> {\n        let mut rx = self.dispatcher.subscribe();\n\n        tokio::spawn(async move {\n            loop {\n                select! {\n                    biased;\n\n                    // React to new events\n                    msg = rx.recv() => match msg {\n                        Ok(env) => {\n                            if let Err(e) = self.process_event(env).await {\n                                tracing::error!(\"BadgeAwardService failed: {e}\");\n                            }\n                        },\n                        Err(broadcast::error::RecvError::Closed) => {\n                            tracing::warn!(\"Dispatcher closed, BadgeAwardService exiting.\");\n                            break;\n                        },\n                        Err(broadcast::error::RecvError::Lagged(skipped)) => {\n                            tracing::warn!(\"BadgeAwardService lagged, skipped {skipped} messages\");\n                        },\n                    },\n\n                    // Allow cooperative cancellation.\n                    _ = tokio::time::sleep(Duration::from_secs(60)) => {},\n                }\n            }\n        })\n    }\n\n    async fn process_event(&self, env: EventEnvelope) -> Result<(), ServiceError> {\n        match env.event {\n            DomainEvent::QuizSubmitted(sub) => self.maybe_award_badge(sub).await?,\n            _ => { /* ignore */ }\n        }\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    async fn maybe_award_badge(&self, sub: QuizSubmitted) -> Result<(), ServiceError> {\n        // Determine qualifying badge.\n        let (badge_id, reason) = if (sub.score - 100.0).abs() < f32::EPSILON {\n            (\n                Uuid::parse_str(\"22222222-2222-2222-2222-222222222222\").unwrap(),\n                \"Perfect quiz score!\".to_owned(),\n            )\n        } else if sub.score >= 90.0 {\n            (\n                Uuid::parse_str(\"11111111-1111-1111-1111-111111111111\").unwrap(),\n                \"Scored 90% or above on a quiz.\".to_owned(),\n            )\n        } else {\n            return Ok(()); // Not eligible\n        };\n\n        // Filter unknown badge IDs (forward-compat).\n        if !self.subscribed_badges.contains(&badge_id) {\n            return Ok(());\n        }\n\n        // Idempotency check: learner may resubmit quiz multiple times.\n        if self\n            .repo\n            .learner_already_has_badge(sub.learner_id, badge_id)\n            .await?\n        {\n            return Ok(());\n        }\n\n        // Compose and persist badge award.\n        let badge = BadgeAwarded {\n            badge_id,\n            learner_id: sub.learner_id,\n            awarded_at: Utc::now(),\n            reason,\n        };\n\n        self.repo.assign_badge(sub.learner_id, &badge).await?;\n\n        let envelope = EventEnvelope::new(DomainEvent::BadgeAwarded(badge.clone()));\n        self.event_store.append(&envelope).await?;\n        self.dispatcher.publish(envelope).await;\n\n        tracing::info!(\n            learner=%sub.learner_id,\n            badge=%badge.badge_id,\n            \"Badge awarded!\"\n        );\n\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n// The code below demonstrates how a single bounded context (\u201clearning pulses\u201d)\n//! reacts to a `SubmissionCreated` domain event and orchestrates **two**\n//! asynchronous side-effects:\n//!   1. A plagiarism check through an external HTTP service.\n//!   2. A rubric-based automatic scoring job.\n//!\n//! Once each task finishes the appropriate *follow-up* event is published so\n//! that other micro-services (notifications, analytics, etc.) can react\n//! independently.\n//!\n//! # Compile features\n//!\n//! - `amqp` \u2013 use a real RabbitMQ event-bus (enabled in CI / prod).\n//! - *none* \u2013 fall back to an in-memory event-bus for local development & tests.\n\nuse std::collections::HashMap;\nuse std::sync::Arc;\nuse std::time::Duration;\n\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse reqwest::StatusCode;\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse thiserror::Error;\nuse tokio::sync::{mpsc, RwLock};\nuse tokio::task::JoinHandle;\nuse tokio::time::timeout;\nuse tracing::{debug, error, info, instrument, warn};\n\n/// Correlation identifier propagated across bounded contexts.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Hash, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct CorrelationId(String);\n\nimpl CorrelationId {\n    pub fn new() -> Self {\n        Self(uuid::Uuid::new_v4().to_string())\n    }\n}\n\n/// A marker trait implemented by *every* domain event.\n///\n/// The obvious choice would be enum-dispatch, however a trait object allows new\n/// events to be added without modifying a central enum \u2013 a desirable property\n/// in a highly modular micro-service code-base.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait DomainEvent: Send + Sync {\n    /// Type discriminator (`\"submission.created\"`, `\"plagiarism.checked\"`, \u2026).\n    fn event_type(&self) -> &'static str;\n\n    /// Monotonic temporal marker.\n    fn occurred_at(&self) -> DateTime<Utc>;\n\n    /// Correlation id used for distributed tracing.\n    fn correlation_id(&self) -> &CorrelationId;\n\n    /// Serialize event instance to JSON for transport on the wire.\n    fn to_json(&self) -> Result<Vec<u8>, EventError> {\n        serde_json::to_vec(self).map_err(EventError::serialization)\n    }\n}\n\n/// Business-level error type for this module.\n#[derive(Debug, Error)]\npub enum EventError {\n    #[error(\"serialization error: {0}\")]\n    Serialization(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"http error: {0}\")]\n    Http(#[from] reqwest::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"event bus error: {0}\")]\n    EventBus(String),\n\n    #[error(\"timeout waiting for plagiarism service\")]\n    TimeOut,\n\n    #[error(\"unexpected response from plagiarism service: {0}\")]\n    InvalidPlagiarismResponse(String),\n}\n\nimpl EventError {\n    fn serialization(err: serde_json::Error) -> Self {\n        Self::Serialization(err)\n    }\n}\n\n/// Concrete domain event &CorrelationId {\n        &self.correlation_id\n    }\n}\n\n/// Event emitted after plagiarism verification finishes.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct PlagiarismChecked {\n    pub submission_id: String,\n    pub similarity_score: f32,\n    pub is_suspect: bool,\n    pub occurred_at: DateTime<Utc>,\n    pub correlation_id: CorrelationId,\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl DomainEvent for PlagiarismChecked {\n    fn event_type(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"plagiarism.checked\"\n    }\n\n    fn occurred_at(&self) -> DateTime<Utc> {\n        self.occurred_at\n    }\n\n    fn correlation_id(&self) -> &CorrelationId {\n        &self.correlation_id\n    }\n}\n\n/// Event emitted after the automatic score is calculated.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct AutoScoreCompleted {\n    pub submission_id: String,\n    pub score: u8,\n    pub rubric_version: String,\n    pub occurred_at: DateTime<Utc>,\n    pub correlation_id: CorrelationId,\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl DomainEvent for AutoScoreCompleted {\n    fn event_type(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"autoscore.completed\"\n    }\n\n    fn occurred_at(&self) -> DateTime<Utc> {\n        self.occurred_at\n    }\n\n    fn correlation_id(&self) -> &CorrelationId {\n        &self.correlation_id\n    }\n}\n\n/// Event bus abstraction.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait EventBus {\n    async fn publish(&self, event: &(dyn DomainEvent + 'static)) -> Result<(), EventError>;\n\n    /// Subscribe with a channel of boxed events.   \n    ///\n    /// In real life we would use strongly typed channels; for brevity we\n    /// down-cast at the consuming site.\n    async fn subscribe(&self) -> mpsc::Receiver<Box<dyn DomainEvent>>;\n}\n\n/// In-memory implementation (dev / tests).\npub struct InMemoryEventBus {\n    tx: mpsc::Sender<Box<dyn DomainEvent>>,\n    rx: RwLock<mpsc::Receiver<Box<dyn DomainEvent>>>,\n}\n\nimpl InMemoryEventBus {\n    pub fn new(buffer: usize) -> Self {\n        let (tx, rx) = mpsc::channel(buffer);\n        Self {\n            tx,\n            rx: RwLock::new(rx),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl EventBus for InMemoryEventBus {\n    async fn publish(&self, event: &(dyn DomainEvent + 'static)) -> Result<(), EventError> {\n        let mut cloned = Vec::new();\n        // Re-serialize to guarantee we send a **copy** (preventing accidental\n        // mutation from other tasks).\n        let bytes = event.to_json()?;\n        let evt_type = event.event_type();\n        cloned.extend_from_slice(&bytes);\n\n        let deserialized: Box<dyn DomainEvent> = match evt_type {\n            \"submission.created\" => {\n                let ev: SubmissionCreated = serde_json::from_slice(&cloned)?;\n                Box::new(ev)\n            }\n            \"plagiarism.checked\" => {\n                let ev: PlagiarismChecked = serde_json::from_slice(&cloned)?;\n                Box::new(ev)\n            }\n            \"autoscore.completed\" => {\n                let ev: AutoScoreCompleted = serde_json::from_slice(&cloned)?;\n                Box::new(ev)\n            }\n            _ => {\n                warn!(\"unrecognized event type on in-memory bus: {evt_type}\");\n                return Ok(());\n            }\n        };\n        self.tx\n            .send(deserialized)\n            .await\n            .map_err(|e| EventError::EventBus(e.to_string()))\n    }\n\n    async fn subscribe(&self) -> mpsc::Receiver<Box<dyn DomainEvent>> {\n        self.rx.write().await.recv().await;\n        // clone underlying channel\n        let mut rx = self.rx.write().await;\n        rx.clone()\n    }\n}\n\n/// Application service orchestrating plagiarism & auto-scoring.\npub struct LearningPulseService {\n    event_bus: Arc<dyn EventBus + Send + Sync>,\n    http: reqwest::Client,\n    plagiarism_endpoint: String,\n    rubric_store: Arc<RubricRepository>,\n}\n\nimpl LearningPulseService {\n    pub fn new(\n        event_bus: Arc<dyn EventBus + Send + Sync>,\n        plagiarism_endpoint: impl Into<String>,\n        rubric_store: Arc<RubricRepository>,\n    ) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            event_bus,\n            http: reqwest::Client::new(),\n            plagiarism_endpoint: plagiarism_endpoint.into(),\n            rubric_store,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Run the long-running background task.\n    pub fn spawn(self: Arc<Self>) -> JoinHandle<()> {\n        tokio::spawn(async move {\n            let mut rx = self.event_bus.subscribe().await;\n            info!(\"learning-pulse service ready to process events\");\n            while let Some(evt) = rx.recv().await {\n                if let Some(submission_evt) = evt.downcast_ref::<SubmissionCreated>() {\n                    let svc = self.clone();\n                    tokio::spawn(async move {\n                        if let Err(err) = svc.process_submission(submission_evt.clone()).await {\n                            error!(?err, \"failed to process submission\");\n                        }\n                    });\n                }\n            }\n        })\n    }\n\n    #[instrument(skip_all, fields(submission_id = %submission.submission_id))]\n    async fn process_submission(&self, submission: SubmissionCreated) -> Result<(), EventError> {\n        let correlation_id = submission.correlation_id.clone();\n\n        // 1) Spawn plagiarism request\n        let plagiarism_future = self\n            .request_plagiarism_check(&submission)\n            .await\n            .map(|res| PlagiarismChecked {\n                submission_id: submission.submission_id.clone(),\n                similarity_score: res.score,\n                is_suspect: res.is_suspect,\n                occurred_at: Utc::now(),\n                correlation_id: correlation_id.clone(),\n            });\n\n        match plagiarism_future {\n            Ok(evt) => {\n                self.event_bus.publish(&evt).await?;\n            }\n            Err(e) => error!(?e, \"plagiarism check failed\"),\n        }\n\n        // 2) Spawn scoring\n        let score_evt = self\n            .auto_score(&submission)\n            .await\n            .map(|score| AutoScoreCompleted {\n                submission_id: submission.submission_id.clone(),\n                score,\n                rubric_version: self.rubric_store.latest_version(),\n                occurred_at: Utc::now(),\n                correlation_id,\n            })?;\n\n        self.event_bus.publish(&score_evt).await?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Calls the external plagiarism API (with timeout protection).\n    async fn request_plagiarism_check(\n        &self,\n        submission: &SubmissionCreated,\n    ) -> Result<PlagiarismResponse, EventError> {\n        #[derive(Serialize)]\n        struct Payload<'a> {\n            submission_id: &'a str,\n            content: &'a str,\n            student_id: &'a str,\n        }\n\n        let body = Payload {\n            submission_id: &submission.submission_id,\n            content: &submission.content,\n            student_id: &submission.author_id,\n        };\n\n        let request = self\n            .http\n            .post(&self.plagiarism_endpoint)\n            .json(&body)\n            .build()?;\n\n        let response = timeout(Duration::from_secs(8), self.http.execute(request)).await;\n\n        let response = match response {\n            Ok(res) => res?,\n            Err(_) => return Err(EventError::TimeOut),\n        };\n\n        if response.status() != StatusCode::OK {\n            return Err(EventError::InvalidPlagiarismResponse(format!(\n                \"status {}\",\n                response.status()\n            )));\n        }\n\n        let result: PlagiarismApiPayload = response.json().await?;\n        Ok(result.into())\n    }\n\n    /// Very naive auto-scoring based on a rubric repository.\n    async fn auto_score(&self, submission: &SubmissionCreated) -> Result<u8, EventError> {\n        let rubric = self.rubric_store.fetch_current().await;\n        let words = submission.content.split_whitespace().count() as u32;\n        let mut score = 0;\n\n        if words >= rubric.min_word_count {\n            score += 60;\n        }\n        if submission.content.contains(\"because\") {\n            score += 15;\n        }\n        if submission.content.contains(\"therefore\") {\n            score += 15;\n        }\n        if submission.content.ends_with('.') {\n            score += 10;\n        }\n        Ok(score.min(100) as u8)\n    }\n}\n\n/// DTO returned from the remote plagiarism service.\n#[derive(Debug, Deserialize)]\nstruct PlagiarismApiPayload {\n    score: f32,\n    is_suspect: bool,\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug)]\nstruct PlagiarismResponse {\n    score: f32,\n    is_suspect: bool,\n}\n\nimpl From<PlagiarismApiPayload> for PlagiarismResponse {\n    fn from(val: PlagiarismApiPayload) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            score: val.score,\n            is_suspect: val.is_suspect,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Simplistic rubric repository.\n/// In production this would talk to Postgres or Config Service.\n#[derive(Default)]\npub struct RubricRepository {\n    current: RwLock<Rubric>,\n}\n\n/// Represents a single rubric configuration.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub struct Rubric {\n    version: String,\n    min_word_count: u32,\n}\n\nimpl RubricRepository {\n    pub async fn fetch_current(&self) -> Rubric {\n        self.current.read().await.clone()\n    }\n\n    pub fn latest_version(&self) -> String {\n        self.current\n            .blocking_read()\n            .version\n            .clone()\n    }\n\n    #[allow(dead_code)]\n    pub async fn update(&self, rubric: Rubric) {\n        *self.current.write().await = rubric;\n    }\n}\n\n//
