body.to_owned(),\n        created_at: Utc::now(),\n        due_at,\n        is_archived: false,\n    };\n\n    self.pulses.insert(&pulse).await?;\n\n    // Fire-and-forget the event\n    self.publisher\n        .publish(PulseEvent::PulseCreated {\n            pulse_id: pulse.id,\n            author_id: pulse.author_id,\n            title: pulse.title.clone(),\n        })\n        .await?;\n\n    Ok(pulse)\n}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### 1. Core Architectural Components Identified\n\n| Component | Module(s) | Technology | Role |\n|-----------|-----------|------------|------|\n| **API Gateway** | module_1, module_49, docs/api.md | Actix-Web / Axum | HTTP/HTTPS endpoint routing, request validation, middleware |\n| **Authentication** | module_1, module_49 | JWT (jsonwebtoken), Argon2, Redis | User registration, login, token validation, session management |\n| **Event Publishing** | module_2, module_4, module_5, module_7 | RabbitMQ (lapin), NATS (async-nats) | Domain event emission to message broker |\n| **Write Model** | module_3, module_10, module_22, module_65 | PostgreSQL (sqlx/diesel) | Command handling, aggregate persistence |\n| **Event Consumers** | module_15, module_68, module_76 | Tokio broadcast, Message broker subscriptions | React to events, update read models, trigger side effects |\n| **Outbox Processor** | module_9, module_11, module_50, module_77 | PostgreSQL + Polling | Reliable at-least-once event delivery |\n\n### 2. Architectural Patterns Identified\n\n**Event-Driven Architecture (EDA)**\n- All state changes emit strongly-typed domain events\n- Events are published to RabbitMQ/NATS for downstream processing\n- Loose coupling between bounded contexts\n\n**CQRS (Command Query Responsibility Segregation)**\n- Evidence: Separate configuration for write database and read-optimized stores\n- Commands (create pulse, submit response) handled by service layer\n- Queries served from denormalized read models (Elasticsearch/MeiliSearch for search)\n\n**Transactional Outbox Pattern**\n- Events persisted in `event_outbox` table within the same database transaction\n- Background `OutboxProcessor` polls for unpublished events and dispatches to broker\n- Guarantees at-least-once delivery without distributed transactions\n\n**Repository Pattern**\n- Abstract `PulseRepository`, `ResponseRepository` traits\n- Concrete PostgreSQL implementations (PgPulseRepository, PgResponseRepository)\n- Enables easy testing with in-memory implementations\n\n**Service Layer Pattern**\n- Business logic encapsulated in services (AuthService, LearningPulseService, BadgeAwardService)\n- Services coordinate repositories, validation, and event emission\n\n### 3. Data Flow: Creating a New Post (Learning Pulse) in a Study Group\n\nSince the codebase uses \"Learning Pulse\" as the primary content entity (similar to a \"Post\" in study groups), I'll trace this flow:\n\n**Step 1: API Request \u2192 API Gateway (module_49)**\n```\nClient \u2192 POST /pulse/response (or /v1/pulses)\n       \u2192 Actix-Web Router extracts JWT from Authorization header\n       \u2192 AuthenticatedUser extractor validates token\n```\n\n**Step 2: Authentication Check (module_1)**\n```\nJWT token \u2192 DecodingKey validation \u2192 Redis session lookup \u2192 User ID extraction\n```\n\n**Step 3: Service Layer Processing (module_22)**\n```\nPulseService.create_pulse(author_id, title, body, due_at)\n  \u2192 Validation (empty title check)\n  \u2192 Create LearningPulse entity with Uuid::new_v4()\n  \u2192 PulseRepository.insert(&pulse) \u2192 PostgreSQL INSERT\n```\n\n**Step 4: Event Emission (module_4 / module_11)**\n```\nEventPublisher.publish(PulseEvent::PulseCreated {...})\n  \u2192 Serialize to JSON\n  \u2192 Insert into event_outbox table (same transaction) OR\n  \u2192 Publish directly to RabbitMQ/NATS\n```\n\n**Step 5: Outbox Processor (module_11 / module_50)**\n```\nOutboxProcessor.tick()\n  \u2192 SELECT * FROM event_outbox WHERE published_at IS NULL\n  \u2192 For each event: nats.publish(subject, payload)\n  \u2192 UPDATE event_outbox SET published_at = NOW()\n```\n\n**Step 6: Event Consumers (module_15 / module_76)**\n```\nSearchIndexer (module_76)\n  \u2192 Subscribe to \"edupulse.web_social.learning_pulse_created\"\n  \u2192 Index document in Elasticsearch/MeiliSearch\n\nBadgeAwardService (module_15)\n  \u2192 Subscribe to relevant events\n  \u2192 Check badge eligibility\n  \u2192 Award badges if criteria met\n```\n\n### 4. Proposed Integration Strategy: Real-time Collaborative Whiteboard\n\n#### New Service Architecture\n\n**WhiteboardService** - New WebSocket-based microservice for real-time drawing collaboration\n\n**Key Design Decisions:**\n\n1. **WebSocket Communication (Not Event Bus)**\n   - Drawing actions require sub-50ms latency\n   - RabbitMQ/NATS adds 10-100ms latency per message hop\n   - Use dedicated WebSocket connections with room-based broadcasting\n\n2. **State Management**\n   - **Hot State**: Redis with Sorted Sets for operation ordering (CRDT-friendly)\n   - **Cold State**: PostgreSQL for persistent whiteboard snapshots\n   - **Snapshotting**: Every N operations or M seconds, persist full state\n\n3. **Authentication Integration**\n   - Reuse existing JWT validation from module_1\n   - WebSocket upgrade requires valid session token\n   - Room access verified against study group membership\n\n4. **Event Bus Integration**\n   - Emit `WhiteboardSessionStarted`, `WhiteboardSessionEnded` to main event bus\n   - Enable downstream analytics, notifications\n   - Main platform stays eventually consistent with whiteboard state\n\n#### Proposed Components\n\n| Component | Technology | Purpose |\n|-----------|------------|---------|\n| **WebSocket Server** | tokio-tungstenite / axum-websocket | Real-time bidirectional communication |\n| **Room Manager** | In-memory HashMap + Redis Pub/Sub | Track connected clients per whiteboard room |\n| **Operation Buffer** | Redis Streams | Order and buffer drawing operations |\n| **Snapshot Store** | PostgreSQL JSONB | Persist whiteboard state periodically |\n| **Auth Middleware** | JWT validation (shared with module_1) | Validate user identity on connect |\n\n#### Data Flow for Drawing Action\n\n```\n1. Client draws \u2192 WebSocket message to WhiteboardService\n2. WhiteboardService validates session, authorizes room access\n3. Operation appended to Redis Stream (whiteboard:{room_id}:ops)\n4. Broadcast operation to all clients in room via WebSocket\n5. Every 30 seconds: Snapshot full canvas state to PostgreSQL\n6. On session end: Emit WhiteboardSessionEnded to RabbitMQ\n```\n\n## MermaidJS Diagrams\n\n### Diagram 1: Existing Architecture (Create Pulse Flow)\n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    subgraph Client\n        A[Web/Mobile Client]\n    end\n\n    subgraph API_Gateway[\"API Gateway (module_49)\"]\n        B[Actix-Web Router]\n        C[JWT Middleware]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Auth[\"Authentication (module_1)\"]\n        D[AuthService]\n        E[Redis Session Store]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Service_Layer[\"Service Layer (module_22)\"]\n        F[PulseService]\n        G[Validation]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Write_Model[\"Write Model\"]\n        H[(PostgreSQL)]\n        I[PulseRepository]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Outbox[\"Outbox (module_11)\"]\n        J[event_outbox table]\n        K[OutboxProcessor]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Message_Broker[\"Message Broker\"]\n        L[RabbitMQ / NATS]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Consumers[\"Event Consumers\"]\n        M[SearchIndexer - module_76]\n        N[BadgeAwardService - module_15]\n        O[AnalyticsWorker]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Read_Model[\"Read Models\"]\n        P[(Elasticsearch)]\n        Q[(Redis Cache)]\n    end\n\n    A -->|POST /v1/pulses| B\n    B --> C\n    C -->|Validate JWT| D\n    D --> E\n    C -->|Authorized| F\n    F --> G\n    G -->|Valid| I\n    I -->|INSERT| H\n    I -->|INSERT| J\n    J --> K\n    K -->|Publish| L\n    L --> M\n    L --> N\n    L --> O\n    M -->|Index| P\n    N -->|Query/Update| H\n```\n\n### Diagram 2: Proposed Architecture with Collaborative Whiteboard\n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    subgraph Client\n        A1[Web Client]\n        A2[Drawing Canvas]\n    end\n\n    subgraph API_Gateway[\"API Gateway (module_49)\"]\n        B[HTTP Router]\n        C[JWT Middleware]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Whiteboard_Service[\"NEW: Whiteboard Service\"]\n        WS1[WebSocket Server]\n        WS2[Room Manager]\n        WS3[Operation Validator]\n        WS4[Broadcast Engine]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Hot_State[\"Hot State\"]\n        HS1[(Redis Pub/Sub)]\n        HS2[(Redis Streams)]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Cold_State[\"Cold State\"]\n        CS1[(PostgreSQL - Snapshots)]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Auth[\"Authentication (module_1)\"]\n        D[AuthService]\n        E[Redis Session Store]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Service_Layer[\"Service Layer (module_22)\"]\n        F[PulseService]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Write_Model[\"Write Model\"]\n        H[(PostgreSQL - Main)]\n        I[PulseRepository]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Outbox[\"Outbox (module_11)\"]\n        J[event_outbox]\n        K[OutboxProcessor]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Message_Broker[\"Message Broker\"]\n        L[RabbitMQ / NATS]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Consumers[\"Event Consumers\"]\n        M[SearchIndexer]\n        N[BadgeAwardService]\n        P[NotificationService]\n    end\n\n    A1 -->|HTTP REST| B\n    B --> C\n    C --> D\n    D --> E\n\n    A2 -->|WebSocket| WS1\n    WS1 -->|Validate Token| D\n    WS1 --> WS2\n    WS2 --> WS3\n    WS3 -->|Buffer Ops| HS2\n    WS3 --> WS4\n    WS4 -->|Broadcast| HS1\n    HS1 -->|Push to Clients| A2\n\n    WS2 -->|Snapshot| CS1\n\n    WS2 -->|Session Events| K\n    K -->|Publish| L\n    L --> P\n\n    C -->|Authorized| F\n    F --> I\n    I --> H\n    I --> J\n    J --> K\n    L --> M\n    L --> N\n```\n\n## Architectural Risks and Bottlenecks\n\n### Risk 1: WebSocket Server as Single Point of Failure (SPOF)\n\n**Description:** The proposed Whiteboard Service introduces a stateful WebSocket server. Unlike the stateless HTTP API which can be horizontally scaled trivially, WebSocket connections maintain persistent state (room membership, connection handles).\n\n**Impact:**\n- If the server crashes, all active whiteboard sessions disconnect\n- Horizontal scaling requires sticky sessions or distributed room management\n- Memory pressure from thousands of concurrent connections\n\n**Mitigation Strategies:**\n1. Deploy behind a WebSocket-aware load balancer (HAProxy, Envoy) with consistent hashing\n2. Use Redis Pub/Sub for cross-instance message propagation\n3. Implement reconnection logic with operation replay from Redis Streams\n4. Consider a CRDT-based state model (e.g., Yjs, Automerge) for conflict-free merge on reconnect\n\n### Risk 2: Eventual Consistency Between Whiteboard and Main Platform\n\n**Description:** The whiteboard operates on a separate data path with Redis as the source of truth for real-time operations. The main PostgreSQL database only receives periodic snapshots.\n\n**Impact:**\n- If snapshot fails, recent drawing operations could be lost\n- Search index and analytics may lag behind actual whiteboard state\n- Race conditions when correlating whiteboard events with other platform events\n\n**Mitigation Strategies:**\n1. Implement Write-Ahead Logging (WAL) to Redis Streams before broadcasting\n2. Use Redis persistence (AOF) for durability\n3. Emit fine-grained events to the main event bus for critical state changes\n4. Design idempotent consumers that handle out-of-order or duplicate events\n\n### Risk 3: Backpressure and Throughput Limits Under High Draw Rate\n\n**Description:** Real-time collaborative drawing can generate hundreds of operations per second per user. With 10 users in a session, this could mean 1000+ messages/second through Redis and WebSocket broadcast.\n\n**Impact:**\n- Redis Pub/Sub has no built-in backpressure; slow consumers drop messages\n- WebSocket send buffers can overflow, causing disconnections\n- Network bandwidth exhaustion on server instances\n\n**Mitigation Strategies:**\n1. **Operation Batching:** Aggregate drawing operations into 16ms (60fps) frames\n2. **Delta Compression:** Send incremental strokes, not full canvas state\n3. **Adaptive Quality:** Reduce precision or sampling rate under load\n4. **Rate Limiting:** Enforce per-user operation limits (e.g., 100 ops/sec max)\n5. **Sharding:** Partition large whiteboards into regions handled by separate processes\n\n## Summary\n\n- **Primary finding**: EduPulse Live follows a well-structured **Event-Driven Architecture** with **CQRS** patterns. The system uses RabbitMQ/NATS as the message broker, PostgreSQL for write models, and Elasticsearch/MeiliSearch for read-optimized search. The **Transactional Outbox** pattern ensures reliable at-least-once event delivery.\n\n- **Key components**:\n  - API Gateway: `module_49.txt` (Actix-Web), `module_1.txt` (Axum)\n  - Authentication: `module_1.txt` (JWT + Redis sessions)\n  - Event Publishing: `module_2.txt`, `module_4.txt`, `module_5.txt` (RabbitMQ/NATS publishers)\n  - Write Model: `module_22.txt`, `module_65.txt` (PostgreSQL repositories)\n  - Event Consumers: `module_15.txt` (Badge awarding), `module_76.txt` (Search indexing)\n  - Outbox Processor: `module_11.txt`, `module_50.txt`, `module_77.txt`\n\n- **Architectural pattern**: Event-Driven Architecture + CQRS + Transactional Outbox + Service-Repository Pattern\n\n- **Recommendations for Whiteboard Integration**:\n  1. Deploy a dedicated WebSocket microservice (tokio-tungstenite) for sub-50ms latency\n  2. Use Redis Streams for operation ordering and Redis Pub/Sub for cross-instance broadcast\n  3. Persist snapshots to PostgreSQL every 30 seconds for durability\n  4. Integrate with existing JWT authentication for session validation\n  5. Emit high-level session events to RabbitMQ for analytics and notifications\n  6. Implement CRDT or OT algorithms for conflict-free collaborative editing\n  7. Plan for horizontal scaling with sticky sessions and distributed room state\n",

Architectural Patterns Identified\n\n**Event-Driven Architecture (EDA)**\n- All state changes emit strongly-typed domain events\n- Events are published to RabbitMQ/NATS for downstream processing\n- Loose coupling between bounded contexts\n\n**CQRS (Command Query Responsibility Segregation)**\n- Evidence: Separate configuration for write database and read-optimized stores\n- Commands (create pulse, submit response) handled by service layer\n- Queries served from denormalized read models (Elasticsearch/MeiliSearch for search)\n\n**Transactional Outbox Pattern**\n- Events persisted in `event_outbox` table within the same database transaction\n- Background `OutboxProcessor` polls for unpublished events and dispatches to broker\n- Guarantees at-least-once delivery without distributed transactions\n\n**Repository Pattern**\n- Abstract `PulseRepository`, `ResponseRepository` traits\n- Concrete PostgreSQL implementations (PgPulseRepository, PgResponseRepository)\n- Enables easy testing with in-memory implementations\n\n**Service Layer Pattern**\n- Business logic encapsulated in services (AuthService, LearningPulseService, BadgeAwardService)\n- Services coordinate repositories, validation, and event emission\n\n### 3. Data Flow: Creating a New Post (Learning Pulse) in a Study Group\n\nSince the codebase uses \"Learning Pulse\" as the primary content entity (similar to a \"Post\" in study groups), I'll trace this flow:\n\n**Step 1: API Request \u2192 API Gateway (module_49)**\n```\nClient \u2192 POST /pulse/response (or /v1/pulses)\n       \u2192 Actix-Web Router extracts JWT from Authorization header\n       \u2192 AuthenticatedUser extractor validates token\n```\n\n**Step 2: Authentication Check (module_1)**\n```\nJWT token \u2192 DecodingKey validation \u2192 Redis session lookup \u2192 User ID extraction\n```\n\n**Step 3: Service Layer Processing (module_22)**\n```\nPulseService.create_pulse(author_id, title, body, due_at)\n  \u2192 Validation (empty title check)\n  \u2192 Create LearningPulse entity with Uuid::new_v4()\n  \u2192 PulseRepository.insert(&pulse) \u2192 PostgreSQL INSERT\n```\n\n**Step 4: Event Emission (module_4 / module_11)**\n```\nEventPublisher.publish(PulseEvent::PulseCreated {...})\n  \u2192 Serialize to JSON\n  \u2192 Insert into event_outbox table (same transaction) OR\n  \u2192 Publish directly to RabbitMQ/NATS\n```\n\n**Step 5: Outbox Processor (module_11 / module_50)**\n```\nOutboxProcessor.tick()\n  \u2192 SELECT * FROM event_outbox WHERE published_at IS NULL\n  \u2192 For each event: nats.publish(subject, payload)\n  \u2192 UPDATE event_outbox SET published_at = NOW()\n```\n\n**Step 6: Event Consumers (module_15 / module_76)**\n```\nSearchIndexer (module_76)\n  \u2192 Subscribe to \"edupulse.web_social.learning_pulse_created\"\n  \u2192 Index document in Elasticsearch/MeiliSearch\n\nBadgeAwardService (module_15)\n  \u2192 Subscribe to relevant events\n  \u2192 Check badge eligibility\n  \u2192 Award badges if criteria met\n```\n\n### 4. Proposed Integration Strategy: Real-time Collaborative Whiteboard\n\n#### New Service Architecture\n\n**WhiteboardService** - New WebSocket-based microservice for real-time drawing collaboration\n\n**Key Design Decisions:**\n\n1. **WebSocket Communication (Not Event Bus)**\n   - Drawing actions require sub-50ms latency\n   - RabbitMQ/NATS adds 10-100ms latency per message hop\n   - Use dedicated WebSocket connections with room-based broadcasting\n\n2. **State Management**\n   - **Hot State**: Redis with Sorted Sets for operation ordering (CRDT-friendly)\n   - **Cold State**: PostgreSQL for persistent whiteboard snapshots\n   - **Snapshotting**: Every N operations or M seconds, persist full state\n\n3. **Authentication Integration**\n   - Reuse existing JWT validation from module_1\n   - WebSocket upgrade requires valid session token\n   - Room access verified against study group membership\n\n4. **Event Bus Integration**\n   - Emit `WhiteboardSessionStarted`, `WhiteboardSessionEnded` to main event bus\n   - Enable downstream analytics, notifications\n   - Main platform stays eventually consistent with whiteboard state\n\n#### Proposed Components\n\n| Component | Technology | Purpose |\n|-----------|------------|---------|\n| **WebSocket Server** | tokio-tungstenite / axum-websocket | Real-time bidirectional communication |\n| **Room Manager** | In-memory HashMap + Redis Pub/Sub | Track connected clients per whiteboard room |\n| **Operation Buffer** | Redis Streams | Order and buffer drawing operations |\n| **Snapshot Store** | PostgreSQL JSONB | Persist whiteboard state periodically |\n| **Auth Middleware** | JWT validation (shared with module_1) | Validate user identity on connect |\n\n#### Data Flow for Drawing Action\n\n```\n1. Client draws \u2192 WebSocket message to WhiteboardService\n2. WhiteboardService validates session, authorizes room access\n3. Operation appended to Redis Stream (whiteboard:{room_id}:ops)\n4. Broadcast operation to all clients in room via WebSocket\n5. Every 30 seconds: Snapshot full canvas state to PostgreSQL\n6. On session end: Emit WhiteboardSessionEnded to RabbitMQ\n```\n\n## MermaidJS Diagrams\n\n### Diagram 1: Existing Architecture (Create Pulse Flow)\n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    subgraph Client\n        A[Web/Mobile Client]\n    end\n\n    subgraph API_Gateway[\"API Gateway (module_49)\"]\n        B[Actix-Web Router]\n        C[JWT Middleware]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Auth[\"Authentication (module_1)\"]\n        D[AuthService]\n        E[Redis Session Store]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Service_Layer[\"Service Layer (module_22)\"]\n        F[PulseService]\n        G[Validation]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Write_Model[\"Write Model\"]\n        H[(PostgreSQL)]\n        I[PulseRepository]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Outbox[\"Outbox (module_11)\"]\n        J[event_outbox table]\n        K[OutboxProcessor]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Message_Broker[\"Message Broker\"]\n        L[RabbitMQ / NATS]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Consumers[\"Event Consumers\"]\n        M[SearchIndexer - module_76]\n        N[BadgeAwardService - module_15]\n        O[AnalyticsWorker]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Read_Model[\"Read Models\"]\n        P[(Elasticsearch)]\n        Q[(Redis Cache)]\n    end\n\n    A -->|POST /v1/pulses| B\n    B --> C\n    C -->|Validate JWT| D\n    D --> E\n    C -->|Authorized| F\n    F --> G\n    G -->|Valid| I\n    I -->|INSERT| H\n    I -->|INSERT| J\n    J --> K\n    K -->|Publish| L\n    L --> M\n    L --> N\n    L --> O\n    M -->|Index| P\n    N -->|Query/Update| H\n```\n\n### Diagram 2: Proposed Architecture with Collaborative Whiteboard\n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    subgraph Client\n        A1[Web Client]\n        A2[Drawing Canvas]\n    end\n\n    subgraph API_Gateway[\"API Gateway (module_49)\"]\n        B[HTTP Router]\n        C[JWT Middleware]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Whiteboard_Service[\"NEW: Whiteboard Service\"]\n        WS1[WebSocket Server]\n        WS2[Room Manager]\n        WS3[Operation Validator]\n        WS4[Broadcast Engine]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Hot_State[\"Hot State\"]\n        HS1[(Redis Pub/Sub)]\n        HS2[(Redis Streams)]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Cold_State[\"Cold State\"]\n        CS1[(PostgreSQL - Snapshots)]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Auth[\"Authentication (module_1)\"]\n        D[AuthService]\n        E[Redis Session Store]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Service_Layer[\"Service Layer (module_22)\"]\n        F[PulseService]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Write_Model[\"Write Model\"]\n        H[(PostgreSQL - Main)]\n        I[PulseRepository]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Outbox[\"Outbox (module_11)\"]\n        J[event_outbox]\n        K[OutboxProcessor]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Message_Broker[\"Message Broker\"]\n        L[RabbitMQ / NATS]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Consumers[\"Event Consumers\"]\n        M[SearchIndexer]\n        N[BadgeAwardService]\n        P[NotificationService]\n    end\n\n    A1 -->|HTTP REST| B\n    B --> C\n    C --> D\n    D --> E\n\n    A2 -->|WebSocket| WS1\n    WS1 -->|Validate Token| D\n    WS1 --> WS2\n    WS2 --> WS3\n    WS3 -->|Buffer Ops| HS2\n    WS3 --> WS4\n    WS4 -->|Broadcast| HS1\n    HS1 -->|Push to Clients| A2\n\n    WS2 -->|Snapshot| CS1\n\n    WS2 -->|Session Events| K\n    K -->|Publish| L\n    L --> P\n\n    C -->|Authorized| F\n    F --> I\n    I --> H\n    I --> J\n    J --> K\n    L --> M\n    L --> N\n```\n\n## Architectural Risks and Bottlenecks\n\n### Risk 1: WebSocket Server as Single Point of Failure (SPOF)\n\n**Description:** The proposed Whiteboard Service introduces a stateful WebSocket server. Unlike the stateless HTTP API which can be horizontally scaled trivially, WebSocket connections maintain persistent state (room membership, connection handles).\n\n**Impact:**\n- If the server crashes, all active whiteboard sessions disconnect\n- Horizontal scaling requires sticky sessions or distributed room management\n- Memory pressure from thousands of concurrent connections\n\n**Mitigation Strategies:**\n1. Deploy behind a WebSocket-aware load balancer (HAProxy, Envoy) with consistent hashing\n2. Use Redis Pub/Sub for cross-instance message propagation\n3. Implement reconnection logic with operation replay from Redis Streams\n4. Consider a CRDT-based state model (e.g., Yjs, Automerge) for conflict-free merge on reconnect\n\n### Risk 2: Eventual Consistency Between Whiteboard and Main Platform\n\n**Description:** The whiteboard operates on a separate data path with Redis as the source of truth for real-time operations. The main PostgreSQL database only receives periodic snapshots.\n\n**Impact:**\n- If snapshot fails, recent drawing operations could be lost\n- Search index and analytics may lag behind actual whiteboard state\n- Race conditions when correlating whiteboard events with other platform events\n\n**Mitigation Strategies:**\n1. Implement Write-Ahead Logging (WAL) to Redis Streams before broadcasting\n2. Use Redis persistence (AOF) for durability\n3. Emit fine-grained events to the main event bus for critical state changes\n4. Design idempotent consumers that handle out-of-order or duplicate events\n\n### Risk 3: Backpressure and Throughput Limits Under High Draw Rate\n\n**Description:** Real-time collaborative drawing can generate hundreds of operations per second per user. With 10 users in a session, this could mean 1000+ messages/second through Redis and WebSocket broadcast.\n\n**Impact:**\n- Redis Pub/Sub has no built-in backpressure; slow consumers drop messages\n- WebSocket send buffers can overflow, causing disconnections\n- Network bandwidth exhaustion on server instances\n\n**Mitigation Strategies:**\n1. **Operation Batching:** Aggregate drawing operations into 16ms (60fps) frames\n2. **Delta Compression:** Send incremental strokes, not full canvas state\n3. **Adaptive Quality:** Reduce precision or sampling rate under load\n4. **Rate Limiting:** Enforce per-user operation limits (e.g., 100 ops/sec max)\n5. **Sharding:** Partition large whiteboards into regions handled by separate processes\n\n## Summary\n\n- **Primary finding**: EduPulse Live follows a well-structured **Event-Driven Architecture** with **CQRS** patterns. The system uses RabbitMQ/NATS as the message broker, PostgreSQL for write models, and Elasticsearch/MeiliSearch for read-optimized search. The **Transactional Outbox** pattern ensures reliable at-least-once event delivery.\n\n- **Key components**:\n  - API Gateway: `module_49.txt` (Actix-Web), `module_1.txt` (Axum)\n  - Authentication: `module_1.txt` (JWT + Redis sessions)\n  - Event Publishing: `module_2.txt`, `module_4.txt`, `module_5.txt` (RabbitMQ/NATS publishers)\n  - Write Model: `module_22.txt`, `module_65.txt` (PostgreSQL repositories)\n  - Event Consumers: `module_15.txt` (Badge awarding), `module_76.txt` (Search indexing)\n  - Outbox Processor: `module_11.txt`, `module_50.txt`, `module_77.txt`\n\n- **Architectural pattern**: Event-Driven Architecture + CQRS + Transactional Outbox + Service-Repository Pattern\n\n- **Recommendations for Whiteboard Integration**:\n  1. Deploy a dedicated WebSocket microservice (tokio-tungstenite) for sub-50ms latency\n  2. Use Redis Streams for operation ordering and Redis Pub/Sub for cross-instance broadcast\n  3. Persist snapshots to PostgreSQL every 30 seconds for durability\n  4. Integrate with existing JWT authentication for session validation\n  5. Emit high-level session events to RabbitMQ for analytics and notifications\n  6. Implement CRDT or OT algorithms for conflict-free collaborative editing\n  7. Plan for horizontal scaling with sticky sessions and distributed room state\n",
